<div id="review_2090310910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2090310910" />
    <a title="Jim Ef" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24950067-jim-ef"><img alt="Jim Ef" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388539229p2/24950067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2090310910?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Ef" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Ef" href="/user/show/24950067-jim-ef">Jim Ef</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2090310910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16617189906260134809">People say the apple doesn’t fall far from the tree. In this case, the apple fell very near indeed, but it got on the ground, grew its own roots and now it stands a proud tree. As you can imagine that is quite an achievement, when the tree that you fell from is named Stephen King.<br/><br/>Before I write my thoughts on this book, I need to tell some very important things. First that not all the stories on this collection, are horror stories. Sure if you must put it in only one category, that would be the </span>
  <span id="freeText16617189906260134809" style="display:none">People say the apple doesn’t fall far from the tree. In this case, the apple fell very near indeed, but it got on the ground, grew its own roots and now it stands a proud tree. As you can imagine that is quite an achievement, when the tree that you fell from is named Stephen King.<br /><br />Before I write my thoughts on this book, I need to tell some very important things. First that not all the stories on this collection, are horror stories. Sure if you must put it in only one category, that would be the one, but I find that unfair. Horror stories make you scared and give you a sense of fear. Those are by far not the only feelings you will get while reading this book. Secondly, here we have a collection of short stories, so they have the pros and cons of short stories. If you are not a fan, it would be better for you to let this one go.<br /><br />I had to choose only three stories to talk about, I would love to share my thoughts of all of them, but it would become quite a big review, not that is a short one now or that someone actually gives a damn about my thoughts.<br /><br />1.Best new horror: A horror magazine publisher reads for a first time in many years an original story. The story is so good but he can’t find the author, so he becomes kind of obsessed. His search finally pays off... although he wish it wouldn’t. The plot is not anything new and the reason I ( and dare I say many people ) don’t enjoy most of the horror fiction (movies or books), is that the genre struggles from originality. Everything is too darn predictable. We know what is going to happen before it does. Imagine how good someone must be to turn this problem into their own favor. Joe Hill is that good. <br />He knows what you are expecting and he drags you there, even when you don’t wanna go anymore, he is still taking you there. It’s like walking on a dark street on a windy night. You know that you are alone, you know that the sounds you hear are coming from the wind. You shouldn’t be scared…. You shouldn’t, but you are.<br /><br />2.Pop Art: Right after I finish reading Pop Art I closed the book. It took me 5 minutes to do something else, to think anything else. I was upset, sad and…and i can’t even describe what was I feeling. Unlike “Best new horror” this is original. Here is the first line of the story “My best friend when I was twelve was inflatable” I thought that this is kind of ridiculous. It took mr.Hill 25 pages to make go from that to what I previously described. This story is a punch right in the heart. <br />(6 stars)<br /><br />3.Voluntary Committal: The last story in this book and what a way to end it. Sometimes it doesn’t matter if you are a kid or an adult. You might know something but you can’t say anything. If you are a kid it’s your imagination, if you are an adult you are crazy. I don’t want to say much about this unique story, so I’ll keep it short. We learn what we learn from Nolan (the narrator) who shortly after his younger brother Morris went missing, got some forgotten memories back. Memories about Eddie, his childhood friend who was last seen back in 1977. He is not sure if the two stories are somehow connected, but even if he was, he couldn’t say anything.<br /><br />It was very hard to choose those three stories so here are the ratings for the rest.<br /><br />20th Century Ghost 4<br />You Will Hear The Locust Sing 4.5 (Kafka was clearly an inspiration for this one)<br />"Abraham's Boys" 4<br />Better Than Home 4.5<br />The Black Phone 5<br />In The Rundown 5<br />The Cape 4<br />Last Breath 4.5<br />"Dead-Wood" 3 (it's only 1 page)<br />"The Widow's Breakfast" 4<br />My Father's Mask 5<br /><br />All I have left to say is, Have a great reading guys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16617189906260134809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3632955178872348918" style="display:none"><b>Pre - Read</b><br><br>This better scare the $#!T out of me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000242038?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Ben</a> , otherwise <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494820925ra/22753384.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>BR starts today!<br><br><br><b> Post Read </b><br><br><br>Heads up: Not so pleasant review. <div id="review_11806974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11806974" />
    <a title="Thomas Gaffney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405856-thomas-gaffney"><img alt="Thomas Gaffney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588897316p2/405856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11806974?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Gaffney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Gaffney" href="/user/show/405856-thomas-gaffney">Thomas Gaffney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405856-thomas-gaffney?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405856-thomas-gaffney?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11806974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15943454400547920700"><i>Best New Horror</i> - Okay. I would have liked to see the story expanded and continued.<br/><i>20th Century Ghost</i> - Really good. A nice, but still creepy, "love" story for horror buffs.<br/><i>Pop Art</i> - The best short story that I have ever read. Can't go into too many details without giving away spoilers.<br/><i>You Will Hear the Locust Sing</i> - Nice story with a 1950s "giant monster" movie feel.<br/><i>Abraham's Boys</i> - Nice "continuing" tale of Van Helsing from Dracula. Good ending.<br/><i>Better Than Home</i> - Eh, sucked.<br/><i>The Black Phone</i> - A</span>
  <span id="freeText15943454400547920700" style="display:none"><i>Best New Horror</i> - Okay. I would have liked to see the story expanded and continued.<br /><i>20th Century Ghost</i> - Really good. A nice, but still creepy, "love" story for horror buffs.<br /><i>Pop Art</i> - The best short story that I have ever read. Can't go into too many details without giving away spoilers.<br /><i>You Will Hear the Locust Sing</i> - Nice story with a 1950s "giant monster" movie feel.<br /><i>Abraham's Boys</i> - Nice "continuing" tale of Van Helsing from Dracula. Good ending.<br /><i>Better Than Home</i> - Eh, sucked.<br /><i>The Black Phone</i> - Another fine, scary story. I feel like Joe Hill, at this point, already does short stories better than his dad.<br /><i>In the Rundown</i> - Okay at best.<br /><i>The Cape</i> - My third fav after Pop Art. Gave me the chills.<br /><i>Last Breath</i> - Very chilling. I would love to see this made into a tv show of some sort.<br /><i>Dead-Wood</i> - Could have saved some trees and done without this one.<br /><i>The Widow's Breakfast</i> - The daughter's were creepy. Would have liked just a story about them.<br /><i>Bobby Conroy Comes Back from the Dead</i> - Eh. One of my least favorite. Seems to just remind the reader that Joe Hill grew up being Stephen King's son.<br /><i>My Father's Mask</i> - WOW. If I hadn't already read Pop Art, then this would be my fav short story. Simply amazing.<br /><i>Voluntary Committal</i> - Nice build up of dread as the story went along, but I felt it was a little dragged out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15943454400547920700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_50844822'>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yoZMS7iSRE30TjtQocXR/Xfvshhj9WnBpL9lK014v2SYC33QhUmtqY1jCKc+lwNjnddrVdh//S4GWA2y9LqxMw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ImUxVd+GTeiLBF0URe8POrENxrlrwIF/9Q3sKQdeJrFw6ADO4l2kDPIpbuPavd2kWzUf9NBKFZBX6oSwvpwo5g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill">About Joe Hill</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1569331514p3/88506.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/88506.Joe_Hill">Joe Hill
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
20,977
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13247810323023463424">Joe Hill's debut, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025._Heart_Shaped_Box' title=' Heart-Shaped Box' rel='nofollow noopener'> Heart-Shaped Box</a>, won the Bram Stoker Award for Best First Novel. His second,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879._Horns' title=' Horns' rel='nofollow noopener'> Horns</a>, was made into a film freakfest starring Daniel Radcliffe. His other novels include <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539._NOS4A2' title=' NOS4A2' rel='nofollow noopener'> NOS4A2</a>, and his #1 New York Times Best-Seller, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25816688._The_Fireman' title=' The Fireman' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Fireman</a>... which was also the winner of a 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Best Horror Novel.<br/><br/>He writes short stories too. Some of them were gathered together in </span>
  <span id="freeText13247810323023463424" style="display:none">Joe Hill's debut, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025._Heart_Shaped_Box" title=" Heart-Shaped Box" rel="nofollow noopener"> Heart-Shaped Box</a>, won the Bram Stoker Award for Best First Novel. His second,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879._Horns" title=" Horns" rel="nofollow noopener"> Horns</a>, was made into a film freakfest starring Daniel Radcliffe. His other novels include <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539._NOS4A2" title=" NOS4A2" rel="nofollow noopener"> NOS4A2</a>, and his #1 New York Times Best-Seller, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25816688._The_Fireman" title=" The Fireman" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Fireman</a>... which was also the winner of a 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Best Horror Novel.<br /><br />He writes short stories too. Some of them were gathered together in his prize-winning collection, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373915._20th_Century_Ghosts" title=" 20th Century Ghosts" rel="nofollow noopener"> 20th Century Ghosts</a>.<br /><br />He won the Eisner Award for Best Writer for his long running comic book series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26225895._Locke___Key" title=" Locke &amp; Key" rel="nofollow noopener"> Locke &amp; Key</a>, co-created with illustrator and art wizard Gabriel Rodriguez.<br /><br />He lives in New Hampshire with a corgi named McMurtry after a certain beloved writer of cowboy tales. His next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30251972._Strange_Weather" title=" Strange Weather" rel="nofollow noopener"> Strange Weather</a>, a collection of novellas, storms into bookstores in October of 2017.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13247810323023463424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
